					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Oirat dialects spoken in Kalmykia, Russia</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Kalmyk language" redirects here. For discussion of the language of the Oirat people in general, see <a href="/wiki/Oirat_language" title="Oirat language">Oirat language</a>.</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above above" style="font-size:125%; <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kalmyk_sign.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kalmyk_sign.jpg/220px-Kalmyk_sign.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kalmyk_sign.jpg/330px-Kalmyk_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kalmyk_sign.jpg/440px-Kalmyk_sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>A bilingual (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> and Kalmyk) sign with the text "Clean zone!" at the <a href="/wiki/Elista" title="Elista">Elista</a> bus station</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Kalmyk Oirat</b> (Kalmyk: <span lang="xal-RU">Хальмг Өөрдин келн</span>, <i>Haľmg Öördin keln</i>, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">IPA:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">&#91;xalʲˈmək<span class="wrap"> </span>øːrˈdin<span class="wrap"> </span>keˈlən&#93;</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> commonly known as the <b>Kalmyk language</b> (Kalmyk: <span lang="xal-RU">Хальмг келн</span>, <i>Haľmg keln</i>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991"><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">IPA:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">&#91;xalʲˈmək<span class="wrap"> </span>keˈlən&#93;</a></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">variety</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Oirat_language" title="Oirat language">Oirat language</a>, natively spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Kalmyks" title="Kalmyks">Kalmyk people</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kalmykia" title="Kalmykia">Kalmykia</a>, a federal subject of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. In Russia, it is the <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">standard form</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Oirat_language" title="Oirat language">Oirat language</a> (based on the <a href="/wiki/Torgut_Oirat" title="Torgut Oirat">Torgut dialect</a>), which belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Mongolic_languages" title="Mongolic languages">Mongolic language family</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kalmyk_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalmyk people">Kalmyk people</a> of the Northwest <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> of Russia claim descent from the <a href="/wiki/Oirats" title="Oirats">Oirats</a> from <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, who have also historically settled in <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwest_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Northwest China">Northwest China</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, the language is "Definitely endangered".<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> According to the Russian census of 2010, there are 80,500 speakers of an <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic group">ethnic population</a> consisting of 183,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kalmyk is now only spoken as a native language by a small minority of the Kalmyk population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Its decline as a <a href="/wiki/Living_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Living language">living language</a> began after the Kalmyk people <a href="/wiki/Kalmyk_deportations_of_1943" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalmyk deportations of 1943">were deported</a> en masse from their homeland in December 1943, as punishment for limited <a href="/wiki/Kalmykian_Voluntary_Cavalry_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalmykian Voluntary Cavalry Corps">Kalmyk collaboration with the Nazis</a>. Significant factors contributing to its demise include: (1) the deaths of a substantial percentage of the Kalmyk population from disease and malnutrition, both during their travel and upon their arrival to remote exile settlements in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, south central <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Far_East" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Far East">Soviet Far East</a>; (2) the wide dispersal of the Kalmyk population; (3) the duration of exile, which ended in 1957; (4) the stigma associated with being accused of treason, and (5) assimilation into the larger, more dominant culture. Collectively, these factors discontinued the intergenerational language transmission.
</p><p>In 1957, the Soviet government reinstated the <a href="/wiki/Kalmyk_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Kalmyk Autonomous Oblast">Kalmyk Autonomous Oblast</a> and later reestablished the <a href="/wiki/Kalmyk_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kalmyk Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Autonomous Republic of Kalmykia</a>. The Kalmyk people were permitted to return to the Republic in 1957, 14 years after exile. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a>, however, was made the official language of the Republic, and Sovietisation was imposed on the Kalmyk people, leading to drastic cuts in Kalmyk language education.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Cyrillic alphabet became firmly established among the Kalmyks (and other peoples, too). For instance, books, periodicals, newspapers, etc., were published using it. By the late 1970s, the Russian language became the primary language of instruction in all schools in the Republic.
</p><p>During the period of <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">Perestroika</a>, Kalmyk linguists, in collaboration with the Kalmyk government, planned and tried to implement the revival of the Kalmyk language. This revival was seen as an integral part of the reassertion of Kalmyk culture. In an important symbolic gesture, the Kalmyk language was declared an official language of the Republic, giving it equal status with the Russian language with respect to official governmental use and language education.
</p><p>During the production of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i>, sound designer Rafe Mercieca—with his life-time partner Ben Curtis—based the language of the <a href="/wiki/Ewok" title="Ewok">Ewoks</a> on Kalmyk after hearing it spoken in a documentary and being impressed with its phonology.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">Geographic distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The majority of Kalmyk language speakers live in the Republic of Kalmykia, where it is an official language. A small group of Kalmyk language speakers also live in France and the US, but the use of Kalmyk is in steep decline. In all three locations, the actual number of speakers is unknown. Kalmyk is an endangered language.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2012, the Kalmyk community in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, which arrived in the US in the 1950s, was planning to work with the <a href="/wiki/Enduring_Voices" title="Enduring Voices">Enduring Voices</a> project to promote Kalmyk language and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistic_classification">Linguistic classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Linguistic classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>From a synchronic perspective, Kalmyk is the most prominent variety of Oirat. It is very close to the Oirat dialects found in Mongolia and the People's Republic of China, both <a href="/wiki/Phonology" title="Phonology">phonologically</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">morphologically</a>. The differences in dialects, however, concern the vocabulary, as the Kalmyk language has been influenced by and has adopted words from the Russian language and various <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic languages</a>.
</p><p>Two important features that characterise Kalmyk are <a href="/wiki/Agglutination" title="Agglutination">agglutination</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">vowel harmony</a>. In an <a href="/wiki/Agglutinative_language" title="Agglutinative language">agglutinative language</a>, words are formed by adding <a href="/wiki/Affixes" class="mw-redirect" title="Affixes">affixes</a> to existing <a href="/wiki/Word" title="Word">words</a>, called stem words or root words. <a href="/wiki/Prefixes" class="mw-redirect" title="Prefixes">Prefixes</a>, however, are not common in Mongolic. Vowel harmony refers to the agreement between the vowels in the root of a word and the vowels in the word's suffix or suffixes. Other features include the absence of <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">grammatical gender</a>.
</p><p>It has some elements in common with the <a href="/wiki/Ugric_languages" title="Ugric languages">Uralic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Uyghur</a> languages, which reflects its origin from the common language of the Oirats, a union of four Oirat tribes that absorbed some Ugric and Turkic tribes during their expansion westward.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Does not provide evidence that similarities with Turkic and Uralic come from the westward expansion of the Oirats and not from earlier contact and/or coincidence (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Similar to <a href="/wiki/Middle_Mongol" title="Middle Mongol">Middle Mongol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Written_Oirat" class="mw-redirect" title="Written Oirat">Written Oirat</a>, Kalmyk exhibits <a href="/wiki/Retracted_tongue_root" class="mw-redirect" title="Retracted tongue root">tongue-root</a> <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">vowel harmony</a>. Unlike <a href="/wiki/Middle_Mongol" title="Middle Mongol">Middle Mongol</a>, however, consonants are not restricted by <a href="/wiki/Consonant_harmony" title="Consonant harmony">harmony</a>. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_fricative" title="Voiced velar fricative">voiced velar fricative</a> /ɣ/ can appear in both front and back vowel words, e.g. һәәвһә /ɣæːwɣæ/ "good" and һалун /ɣalun/ "goose".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, all consonants and <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">neutral reduced vowel</a> /ə/ are influenced by harmonic status of a word, at least phonetically. The harmonic vowel pairs are: /a/~/æ/, /o/~/ø/, /u/~/y/, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">i</a>&#93;</span>~<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Close central unrounded vowel">ɨ</a>&#93;</span>, the last pair being <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophonic</a>.
</p><p>Historical <a href="/wiki/Long_vowels" class="mw-redirect" title="Long vowels">long vowels</a> in non-initial syllables have been reduced to <a href="/wiki/Short_vowels" class="mw-redirect" title="Short vowels">short vowels</a>, while historical short vowels have been reduced to <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a> and then, just like in <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>, were replaced according to language's <a href="/wiki/Phonotactics" title="Phonotactics">phonotactics</a>. For example, <a href="/wiki/Written_Oirat" class="mw-redirect" title="Written Oirat">Written Oirat</a> <i>ɣarān</i> "hand-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possesive reflexive" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">P.REFL</abbr>" became һаран /ɣaran/; <i>ɣarɣaqsan</i> "to get out-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="causative" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CAUS</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past participle" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PC.PST</abbr>" became һарһсн /ɣarɣsən/. Long vowels and <a href="/wiki/Diphthongs" class="mw-redirect" title="Diphthongs">diphthongs</a> in one-syllable words have been also reduced to short vowels: <i>sayin</i> "good" &gt; сән /sæn/. Nevertheless, in inflected forms of such words, short vowels tend to become elongated: сән /sæn/ "good" &gt; сәәг /sæːgə/ "good-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr>", күн /kyn/ "man"&gt; күүнә /kyːnæ/ "man-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="genitive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">GEN</abbr>". Despite that, long vowels still may be pronounced in non-initial syllables. This happens if a word consists of three syllables, second of which has a vowel /a/ or /æ/, and third syllable has a <a href="/wiki/Reduced_vowel" class="mw-redirect" title="Reduced vowel">reduced vowel</a> /ə/. Examples include гөрәсн [gøræːsᵊn] "<a href="/wiki/Saiga" class="mw-redirect" title="Saiga">saiga</a>", туршарт [turʃaːrtə] "during", кезәңк [kezæːŋkə] "a while ago", һазрас [ɢazraːsə] "land-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ablative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABL</abbr>".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">Consonants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Consonants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following is an outline of the consonant system of Kalmyk. Note that since virtually all speakers of Kalmyk are <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> recent borrowings from <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> do not undergo phonological adaptation and are pronounced according to the rules of <a href="/wiki/Russian_phonology" title="Russian phonology">Russian phonology</a>, including those of <a href="/wiki/Vowel_reduction_in_Russian" title="Vowel reduction in Russian">vowel reduction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_phonology#Stress" title="Russian phonology">stress</a>.
</p>

<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_labiodental_fricative" title="Voiceless labiodental fricative">voiceless labiodental fricative</a> /f/ occurs only in loanwords and <a href="/wiki/Onomatopoeic" class="mw-redirect" title="Onomatopoeic">onomatopoeic</a> terms;</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_fricative" title="Voiced velar fricative">voiced velar fricative</a> /ɣ/ may also be released as a uvular plosive <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_uvular_plosive" title="Voiced uvular plosive">ɢ</a>&#93;</span> in the word-initial position as well as uvular fricative <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_uvular_fricative" title="Voiced uvular fricative">ʁ</a>&#93;</span> in any position, including initial;</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">voiceless velar fricative</a> /x/ may also be pronounced as <a href="/wiki/Uvular" class="mw-redirect" title="Uvular">uvular</a> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">χ</a>&#93;</span>;</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Voiced_labial%E2%80%93velar_approximant" title="Voiced labial–velar approximant">voiced labial approximant</a> /w/ may be released as the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_fricative" title="Voiced bilabial fricative">voiced bilabial fricative</a> [β];<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" class="mw-redirect" title="Velar nasal">velar nasal</a> /ŋ/ is often pronounced with a velar plosive <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_plosive" title="Voiced velar plosive">g</a>&#93;</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_plosive" title="Voiceless velar plosive">k</a>&#93;</span> at the end, e.g. дөң [døŋk] "help", саң [saŋk] "treasury", маңна [maŋgna] "forehead".</li></ul>

<ul><li>Note that the mid central vowel /<a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">ə</a>/ is not orthographically written;</li>
<li>The open back vowel is also phonetically central <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Open central unrounded vowel">ä</a>&#93;</span>;</li>
<li>The (historically reduced) vowel /ə/ is phonetically released as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Relative_articulation#Advanced_and_retracted" title="Relative articulation">ə̟</a>&#93;</span> in <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">harmonically</a> front-vowel words, as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Relative_articulation#Advanced_and_retracted" title="Relative articulation">ə̠</a>&#93;</span> in back-vowel words, and as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Near-close_near-front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-close near-front unrounded vowel">ɪ</a>&#93;</span> after palatal and post-alveolar consonants /nʲ tʲ dʲ t͡ɕ d͡ʑ ʃ lʲ j/;<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Although not always manifested orthographically, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Close central unrounded vowel">ɨ</a>&#93;</span> is a back vowel word allophone of /i/ that is only present in <a href="/wiki/Hortative" title="Hortative">hortative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genitive" class="mw-redirect" title="Genitive">genitive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accusative" class="mw-redirect" title="Accusative">accusative</a> suffixes;<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In native words, vowels /o oː/ and /ø øː/ can only appear in word-initial syllables.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Devoicing_and_assimilation">Devoicing and assimilation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Devoicing and assimilation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Orthographic <a href="/wiki/Voicing_(phonetics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Voicing (phonetics)">voiced</a> <a href="/wiki/Plosive" title="Plosive">stops</a> d, g are devoiced: келәд /kelæt/ "to speak-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="anterior converb" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CV.ANT</abbr>", бөлг /bølək/ "chapter". <a href="/wiki/Devoicing" class="mw-redirect" title="Devoicing">Devoicing</a> also occurs whenever there is a two-consonant <a href="/wiki/Consonant_cluster" title="Consonant cluster">cluster</a> with one consonant being <a href="/wiki/Voiceless" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless">voiceless</a>: /bolʃko/ "may not", таңһч /taŋxt͡ɕə/ "republic". Consonant clusters exhibit other types of assimilation:
</p>
<ol><li>/kx/, /gx/, /xx/ &gt; /kk/, /kk/, /xk/: закх /zakxə~zakkə/ "to order"; өргх /ørkxə~ørkkə/ "to raise" хатхх /xatxxə~xatxkə/ "to poke";</li>
<li>/n/ + /b/ &gt; /mb/: кен /ken/ "who" + б /bə/ "<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="question word" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">Q</abbr>" &gt; кемб /kembə/ "who-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="question word" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">Q</abbr>";</li>
<li>/w/ + /n/ &gt; /mn/: тәв- /tæv-/ "to put" + /-næ/ "<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="present tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PRS</abbr>" &gt; тәмнә /tæmnæ/ "to put-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="present tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PRS</abbr>";</li>
<li>/w/ + <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless consonant">voiceless consonant</a> &gt; /p/: ав- /awə/ "to take" + чк /t͡ɕkə/ "<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="completive aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">COMPL</abbr>&gt; апчк /apt͡ɕkə/ "to put-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="completive aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">COMPL</abbr>";</li>
<li>/t͡ɕ/ + /l/ or /t/ &gt; /ʃl/, /ʃt/: көвүчлх /køvyt͡ɕəlxə/ &gt; көвүшлх /køvyʃəlxə/ "to adopt", ачтн /at͡ɕtən/ &gt; аштн /aʃtən/ "to load-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural imperative" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">IMP.PL</abbr>"&#160;;</li>
<li>/n/ &gt; /ŋ/ before consonants /ɣ, g, x, k, s/: <a href="/wiki/Written_Oirat" class="mw-redirect" title="Written Oirat">Written Oirat</a> <i>sonosxu</i> "to listen" &gt; соңсх /soŋksxə/, түрүн /tyryn/ "first" + к /kə/ "<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="adjective" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ADJ</abbr>" &gt; түрүңк /tyryŋkə/ "first-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="adjective" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ADJ</abbr>";</li>
<li>/l/ is <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">palatalised</a> to /lʲ/ before <a href="/wiki/Palatal" class="mw-redirect" title="Palatal">palatal</a> <a href="/wiki/Affricates" class="mw-redirect" title="Affricates">affricates</a> /t͡ɕ d͡ʑ/: болҗ /bolʲd͡ʑə/ "to become-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="imperfective converb" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CV.IPEF</abbr>".</li></ol>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_stop" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced bilabial stop">voiced bilabial stop</a> /b/, being only restricted to word-initial position, may be pronounced as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_fricative" title="Voiced bilabial fricative">β</a>&#93;</span> in a phrase: келҗ бәәнә /kelʲd͡ʑə bæːnæ/ &gt; [kelʲd͡ʑ βæːnæ] "to speak-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="imperfective converb" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CV.IPEF</abbr> to be-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="present tense">prs</abbr>".
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Voiced_labial%E2%80%93velar_approximant" title="Voiced labial–velar approximant">labial approximant</a> or <a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_fricative" title="Voiced bilabial fricative">fricative</a> /w/ can be pronounced as:
</p>
<ol><li>Close rounded <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">vowel</a> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_front_rounded_vowel" title="Close front rounded vowel">y</a>&#93;</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">u</a>&#93;</span> in past tense <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">inflection</a>: кел- /kelʲ-/ "to say" + -в /w/ "<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PST</abbr>" + -в /w/ "<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr>" &gt; келүв /kelyw/ "I said" or in consonant clusters: тарвс /tarvəs/ &gt; тарус /tarus/ "watermelon"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_stop" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced bilabial stop">Voiced bilabial stop</a> [b] in <a href="/wiki/Past_tense" title="Past tense">past tense</a> inflection, if the <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">verb</a> <a href="/wiki/Stem_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stem (linguistics)">stem</a> ends in /-w/: ав- /aw-/ "to take" + -в /-w/ "<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PST</abbr>" &gt; /awbə/ "took".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowel_reduction_and_phonotactics">Vowel reduction and phonotactics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Vowel reduction and phonotactics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Word-initial <a href="/wiki/Syllable_structure" class="mw-redirect" title="Syllable structure">syllable structure</a> is (C)V(C), meaning that in native words no word-initial clusters can occur. For non-initial syllables, however, a syllable-initial cluster of up to four consonants is allowed, meaning the maximal syllable is CCCCVC. In some <a href="/wiki/Consonant_clusters" class="mw-redirect" title="Consonant clusters">consonant clusters</a> such as /tl tn dn dl/ a <a href="/wiki/Sonorant" title="Sonorant">sonorant</a> becomes <a href="/wiki/Syllabic_consonant" title="Syllabic consonant">syllabic</a>. These clusters are also <a href="/wiki/Nasal_release" title="Nasal release">nasally released</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vowel_reduction" title="Vowel reduction">The reduced vowel</a> /ə/ is regularly preserved and can be a <a href="/wiki/Syllable_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Syllable nucleus">syllable nucleus</a> in the following cases:
</p>
<ol><li>In a word-final position: ик /i.kə/ "big", арат /a.ra.tə/ "fox", чон /t͡ɕo.nə/ "wolf";</li>
<li>If, word-finally, there is either a <a href="/wiki/Closed_syllable" class="mw-redirect" title="Closed syllable">closed syllable</a> or a final <a href="/wiki/Open_syllable" class="mw-redirect" title="Open syllable">open syllable</a> with a consonant cluster: эцкнр /et͡s.kə.nər/ "father-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr>" келчксн /kelʲ.t͡sək.sən/ "to say-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="completive aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">COMPL</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past participle" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PC.PST</abbr>" соңсгдна /soŋk.sə.gdna/ "to hear-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="passive voice" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PASS</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="present tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PRS</abbr>";</li>
<li>In closed non-final syllables of a multisyllabic word: шорһлҗн /ʃor.ɣəlʲ.d͡ʑən/ "ant", әәмшгтә /æ:m.ʃək.tæ/ "dangerous";<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Word-finally in the following affixes:
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Ablative" class="mw-redirect" title="Ablative">Ablative</a> -ас /-asə/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Accusative" class="mw-redirect" title="Accusative">Accusative</a> -иг /-igə/, -г /-gə/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adjective" title="Adjective">Adjective suffix</a> -к /-kə/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">Completive</a> -чк /-t͡ɕkə/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Converb" title="Converb">Imperfective converb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Admirative" class="mw-redirect" title="Admirative">admirative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evidential" class="mw-redirect" title="Evidential">evidential</a> suffix -җ /-dʑə/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dative" class="mw-redirect" title="Dative">Dative</a> -д /-də/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Negation" title="Negation">Negation</a> particle эс /esə/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Present_tense" title="Present tense">Present tense</a> <a href="/wiki/Negation" title="Negation">negation</a> particle (or <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffix</a>) биш, -ш /biʃə/ /-ʃə/;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Future_tense" title="Future tense">Future tense</a> <a href="/wiki/Participle" title="Participle">participle</a> -х /-xə/.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li></ol></li></ol>
<p>On the other hand, the vowel /ə/ cannot form syllables on its own if the following is true:
</p>
<ol><li>If the following syllable is <a href="/wiki/Open_syllable" class="mw-redirect" title="Open syllable">open</a>: бичх /bi.t͡ɕxə/ "to write", өгх /øk.kxə/ "to give";</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Inflections" class="mw-redirect" title="Inflections">inflections</a> of two-syllable words, if the second syllable of an inflected word has a non-reduced vowel, e.g. мөрн /mørən/ "horse" &gt; мөрта mørtæ "with a horse", церг /t͡se.rək/ "army" &gt; церглә  /t͡serglæ/ "with an army";</li>
<li>If the following syllable is open and has non-reduced vowel: тоһрун */to.ɣə.run/ &gt; /to.ɣrun/ "grus"; шамдһа */ʃam.də.ɣa/ &gt; /ʃam.dɣa/ "sneaky". In this case, however, reduced syllables may be released phonetically, although they do not play a role in <a href="/wiki/Syllable_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Syllable nucleus">syllable forming</a>.;<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>Two-syllable words with schwa as a <a href="/wiki/Syllable_nucleus" class="mw-redirect" title="Syllable nucleus">nucleus</a> of the second syllable may undergo <a href="/wiki/Metathesis_(linguistics)" title="Metathesis (linguistics)">metathesis</a>, thus creating an <a href="/wiki/Open_syllable" class="mw-redirect" title="Open syllable">open syllable</a>: <a href="/wiki/Written_Oirat" class="mw-redirect" title="Written Oirat">Written Oirat</a> <i>oros</i> "Russian" &gt; /orəs/ &gt; /orsə/; <i>ulus</i> "country, people" &gt; /uləs/ &gt; /ulsə/; <i>oyirad</i> "Oirat" &gt; /øːrət/ &gt; /øːrdə/.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stress">Stress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stress"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kalmyk exhibits <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)#Non-phonemic_stress" title="Stress (linguistics)">non-phonemic stress</a> with the last syllable (even if it ends in <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a>) being stressed.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Like other <a href="/wiki/Mongolic_languages" title="Mongolic languages">Mongolic languages</a>, Kalmyk is an <a href="/wiki/Agglutinative" class="mw-redirect" title="Agglutinative">agglutinative</a>, suffixing, and a <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">genderless</a> language. Some aspects of its <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntax</a> have been influenced by <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>; for example, <a href="/wiki/Relative_clause" title="Relative clause">relative clauses</a>, traditionally characterized by <a href="/wiki/Branching_(linguistics)" title="Branching (linguistics)">left-branching</a> and employing a <a href="/wiki/Converb" title="Converb">converbial form</a> of a verb (similarly to <a href="/wiki/Japanese_grammar" title="Japanese grammar">Japanese</a>), now often use Russian relative pronoun <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%B9" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:который">который</a> and thus exhibit right-branching. Other noticeable feature possibly influenced by Russian is frequent usage of future <a href="/wiki/Participle" title="Participle">participle</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Predicate_(grammar)" title="Predicate (grammar)">predicate</a> of a sentence to express <a href="/wiki/Future_tense" title="Future tense">future tense</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> There is little to none <a href="/wiki/Suppletion" title="Suppletion">suppletion</a> (irregular forms) in verbal <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">inflection</a> and noun <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_conjugation" title="Grammatical conjugation">conjugation</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns">Nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Nouns"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Traditionally, Kalmyk <a href="/wiki/Case_(grammar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Case (grammar)">cases</a> are said to have three declensions; however, this is mostly due to orthographical peculiarities. Basically, if the word ends in a full vowel and the case ending begins in a vowel, either (1) a prothetic /g/ or /ʁ/ is added or (2) a vowel is deleted from the case ending. This is further demonstrated in the table below.
</p>
<dl><dd><table class="wikitable">

<caption>Kalmyk noun cases <sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Case</th>
<th>Suffix (Cyrillic)</th>
<th>Suffix (IPA)</th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Clear_Script" title="Clear Script">Clear Script</a> spelling
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Nominative_case" title="Nominative case">nominative</a></td>
<td>-∅</td>
<td>-∅</td>
<td>-
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive</a></td>
<td>-ин; -һин; -н; -а; -ә; -i</td>
<td>-in; -ʁin; -n; -a; -æ; -i</td>
<td><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr;  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡅ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-i</i></span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Dative_case" title="Dative case">dative</a></td>
<td>-д; -т</td>
<td>-də; -tə</td>
<td><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡑᡇ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-du</i></span>) / <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡑᡉ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-dü</i></span>) (depending on <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">vowel harmony</a>) <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡐᡇ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-tu</i></span>) / <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡐᡉ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-tü</i></span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">accusative</a></td>
<td>-иг; -г; ∅</td>
<td>-igə; -gə; ∅</td>
<td><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡕᡅᡎᡅ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-yigi</i></span>); <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡎᡅ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-gi</i></span>); -
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ablative_case" title="Ablative case">ablative</a></td>
<td>-ас; -әс; -һас; -һәс</td>
<td>-asə; -æsə; -ʁasə; -ʁæsə</td>
<td><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᠠᡃᠰᠠ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-āsa</i></span>), <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡄᡃᠰᡄ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-ēse</i></span>) (later spelling, written together with the word); <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡄᡃᡔᡄ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-ēce</i></span>) (earlier spelling, written separately from the word)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Instrumental_case" title="Instrumental case">instrumental</a></td>
<td>-ар; -әр; -һар; -һәр</td>
<td>-ar; -ær; ʁar; ʁær</td>
<td><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᠠᡃᠷ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-ār</i></span>), <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡄᡃᠷ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-ēr</i></span>); <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡅᡕᠠᠷ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-iyar</i></span>) (earlier spelling)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Comitative_case" title="Comitative case">comitative</a></td>
<td>-та; -тә</td>
<td>-ta; -tæ</td>
<td><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡐᠠᡅ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-tai</i></span>); <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡐᡄᡅ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-tei</i></span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Allative_case" title="Allative case">directive</a></td>
<td>-ур; -үр; -һур; -һүр</td>
<td>-ur; -yr; -ʁur; -ʁyr</td>
<td><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡇᡇᠷ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-uur</i></span>); <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1161532786"><span class="font-mong" style="display:inline-block; font-weight:normal; font-size: 1.25em; line-height: 1.2em; -webkit-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -o-writing-mode: vertical-lr; -ms-writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: tb-lr; writing-mode: vertical-lr;; text-orientation: sideways; vertical-align:text-top;">ᡇᡇᠷᡇ</span> (<span title="Written Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xwo-Latn">-uuru</i></span>) (earlier spelling; written separately from the word)
</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">Genitive</a> takes the suffix -ин (<span title="Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xal-Latn">-in</i></span>) in case it is preceded by a consonant; -һин (<span title="Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xal-Latn">-ğin</i></span>) or -н (<span title="Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xal-Latn">-n</i></span>) if it is preceded by a vowel; -ә (<span title="Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xal-Latn">-ä</i></span>), -a or -и (<span title="Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xal-Latn">-i</i></span>) if it is preceded by the /n/ consonant.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dative_case" title="Dative case">Dative</a> suffix is -т (<span title="Oirat-language romanization"><i lang="xal-Latn">-t</i></span>) if preceded by voiced stops /b/ (/β/) /d/ /g/, voiceless sibilants /s/ /ʃ/, and /r/</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">Accusative</a> is marked (with a suffix) if the object is definite, unmarked if the object is indefinite</li>
<li>Nouns ending in -n declense differently. -n is subtracted in the accusative, instrumental, and comitative cases. In all other cases, it is left untouched. For example: kelʲən "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="nominative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">NOM</abbr>" kelʲnæ "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="genitive case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">GEN</abbr>" kelʲəndə "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="dative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DAT</abbr>" kelʲə/kelʲigə "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr>" kelʲnæsə "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="ablative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ABL</abbr>" kelʲær "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="instrument(al)" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INS</abbr>" kelʲtæ "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="comitative case (&#39;together with&#39;)" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">COM</abbr>" kelʲnyr "language-<abbr class="gloss-abbr gloss-abbr-ambiguous" title="directive (lative) case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DIR</abbr>"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dative" class="mw-redirect" title="Dative">Dative</a> also bears the function of <a href="/wiki/Lative" class="mw-redirect" title="Lative">lative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Locative" class="mw-redirect" title="Locative">locative</a> cases. Its difference with the <a href="/wiki/Illative" class="mw-redirect" title="Illative">directive</a> case is not clear, and in some dialects, <a href="/wiki/Dative" class="mw-redirect" title="Dative">dative</a> is  the prevailing case for <a href="/wiki/Lative" class="mw-redirect" title="Lative">lative</a> usage.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_systems">Writing systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Writing systems"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Clear-script-19th-ctry.png" class="mw-file-description" title="Todo bichig"><img alt="Todo bichig" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Clear-script-19th-ctry.png/200px-Clear-script-19th-ctry.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="108" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Clear-script-19th-ctry.png/300px-Clear-script-19th-ctry.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Clear-script-19th-ctry.png/400px-Clear-script-19th-ctry.png 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="756" /></a><figcaption>Todo bichig</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Clear_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Clear script">Clear script</a></div>
<p>The literary tradition of Oirat reaches back to 11th century when the <a href="/wiki/Old_Uyghur_alphabet" title="Old Uyghur alphabet">Old Uyghur script</a> was used. The official Kalmyk alphabet, named <a href="/wiki/Clear_Script" title="Clear Script">Clear Script</a> or <i>Todo bichig</i> in Oirat, was created in the 17th century by a Kalmyk Buddhist monk called <a href="/wiki/Zaya_Pandita" title="Zaya Pandita">Zaya Pandita</a>.
</p><p>Like the Old Mongolian script, Todo bichig was written from top to bottom. Written Oirat language contained many words borrowed from the Mongolian language and not used in everyday speech, despite many attempts to bring the written standard and colloquial spoken language closer together. Thus, already at the beginning of the 18th century, two written forms of the Kalmyk language were recorded - “bookish”, used in religious practice and having numerous Mongolian and Tibetan borrowings and preserving archaic language forms, as well as “conversational”, used in private correspondence and reflecting the changes taking place in the language<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов19766–11_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов19766–11-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed. (January 2021)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Todo bichig, also called “zayapandit script” after its creator, existed among the Kalmyks until 1924 with minor changes. Oirats of China use it to the present.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1924 this script was replaced by an adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic script</a>, which was abandoned in 1930 in favour of a <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Cyrillic_alphabets">Early Cyrillic alphabets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Early Cyrillic alphabets"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the end of the 19th and the beginning of the 20th centuries, the Orthodox Missionary Society published a number of school books in the Kalmyk language, using Cyrillic script. The first edition of this kind was the "Primer for Kalmyk ulus schools" (1892). The alphabet used in this primer has the following composition: <b>А а, Б б, В в, Г г, Д д, Е е, З з, И и, К к, Л л, М м, Н н, О о, П п, Р р, С с, Т т, У у, Х х, Ц ц, Ч ч, Ш ш, ь, Э э, Ю ю, Я я, <a href="/wiki/%D3%92" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӓ">Ӓ</a> <a href="/wiki/%D3%92" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӓ">ӓ</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%80" title="Ā">Ā</a> <a href="/wiki/%C4%80" title="Ā">ā</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C7%9E" class="mw-redirect" title="Ǟ">Ǟ</a> <a href="/wiki/%C7%9E" class="mw-redirect" title="Ǟ">ǟ</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D3%A6" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӧ">Ӧ</a> <a href="/wiki/%D3%A6" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӧ">ӧ</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%8C" class="mw-redirect" title="Ō">Ō</a> <a href="/wiki/%C5%8C" class="mw-redirect" title="Ō">ō</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C8%AA" class="mw-redirect" title="Ȫ">Ȫ</a> <a href="/wiki/%C8%AA" class="mw-redirect" title="Ȫ">ȫ</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D3%B0" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӱ">Ӱ</a> <a href="/wiki/%D3%B0" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӱ">ӱ</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D3%AE" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӯ">Ӯ</a> <a href="/wiki/%D3%AE" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӯ">ӯ</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=%D3%B0%CC%84&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ӱ̄ (page does not exist)">Ӱ̄</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=%D3%B0%CC%84&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ӱ̄ (page does not exist)">ӱ̄</a>, Д<a href="/wiki/%D0%96" class="mw-redirect" title="Ж">ж</a> д<a href="/wiki/%D0%96" class="mw-redirect" title="Ж">ж</a>, Нг нг, <a href="/wiki/%D0%86" class="mw-redirect" title="І">І</a>й, <a href="/wiki/%D0%86" class="mw-redirect" title="І">і</a>й, Йе йе, Йӧ йӧ, Ӓй ӓй, <a href="/wiki/%D3%A2" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӣ">Ӣ</a> <a href="/wiki/%D3%A2" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӣ">ӣ</a>, Э̄ э̄, Ю̄ ю̄, Я̄ я̄</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 1902, the “Primer for Kalmyks” was released, where a different version of the alphabet was used: <b>А а, Б б, Г г, Д д, З з, И и, Й й, К к, Л л, М м, Н н, О о, Р р, С с, Т т, У у, Х х, Ц ц, Ч ч, Ш ш, ь, Э э, Ӓ ӓ, Ā ā, Ǟ ǟ, Ӧ ӧ, Ō ō, Ȫ ȫ, Ӱ ӱ, Ӯ ӯ, Ӱ̄ ӱ̄, Дж дж, Ҥ ҥ, Ӣ ӣ, Э̄ э̄</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, the letter of the clear script continued to be used.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 6, 1924, a meeting of the Kalmyk public was held in Astrakhan. At this meeting, the majority of the votes had declared obsolete writing - it was noted that it was difficult for writing and learning, lack of fonts, the inability to use on the telegraph, and so on. In this regard, it was decided to translate Kalmyk language into Cyrillic script. On January 12, the alphabet was adopted, consisting of the following letters: <b>А а, Б б, В в, Г г, Д д, Е е, Ж ж, З з, И и, К к, Л л, М м, Н н, О о, П п, Р р, С с, Т т, У у, Ф ф, Х х, Ц ц, Ч ч, Ш ш, Щ щ, Ы ы, Э э, Ю ю, Я я, Ь ь, Й й, <a href="/wiki/%C3%84" title="Ä">ä</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%96" title="Ö">ö</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D3%B0" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӱ">ӱ</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D2%A2" class="mw-redirect" title="Ң">ң</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D3%9C" class="mw-redirect" title="Ӝ">ӝ</a></b>. Above the long vowels was supposed to put a line (macron), but in practice this was not done. Also, despite the absence of an approved project, the letter <b>ъ</b> was used to designate unclear vowels. From January 1926, the newspaper <b><a href="/w/index.php?title=Halmg_unn_(newspaper)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Halmg unn (newspaper) (page does not exist)">«Ulan Halmg»</a></b> (<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BC%D0%B3_%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BD" class="extiw" title="ru:Хальмг унн">ru</a>) began to be printed on this alphabet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197652–54_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197652–54-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The basis of the emerging Kalmyk literary language was the Torgut dialect, but later the norm began to focus not only on the Torgut, but also on the Derbet dialect.<sup id="cite_ref-Пям_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Пям-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Sometimes in the editions of that time, the letter <i>ң</i> was replaced by <b>ҥ</b> or <b>н̈</b>, and the letters <i>Е е, Ж ж, Ф Ф, Щ щ</i> were not officially included in the alphabet.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>September 7, 1926 at a meeting at the Kalmyk pedagogical school in Astrakhan, it was decided to make changes to the alphabet. So, all additional letters were canceled, and instead of them entered <b>D d, V v, H h</b>. In June 1927, this alphabet was introduced into official use, but much of the literature and press was still published in the alphabet of 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197660–64_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197660–64-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 5–8, 1928, a regular meeting on Kalmyk writing was held, at which the alphabet was reformed again. The letters <i>D d, V v, H h</i> were canceled, and the letter <b>Ә ә</b> was entered to indicate unclear vowels. It was decided to denote the long vowels by doubling the corresponding letters. This alphabet was used until 1930.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197668–70_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197668–70-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_alphabet">Latin alphabet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Latin alphabet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the late 1920s, the process of <a href="/wiki/Latinisation_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Latinisation in the Soviet Union">romanization of writing</a> began in the USSR. In the course of this process in January 1930, the IX Kalmyk Regional Congress of Soviets legalized the new Latinized alphabet of the Kalmyk language. Its actual use began in newspapers from the end of September of the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197678–79_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197678–79-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In this alphabet, the letters were arranged in the following order:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197679_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197679-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <b>A a, B b, C c, Ç ç, D d, E e, Ә ә, G g, H h, I i, j, K k, L l, M m, N n, ꞑ, O o, Ө ө, P p, R r, S s, Ş ş, F f, Y y, Z z, Ƶ ƶ, U u, T t, V v, X x, ь</b>.
</p><p>On January 10–17, 1931, at a conference held in Moscow, scientists of the Mongolian group of peoples decided to change the phonetic meaning of the two letters of the Kalmyk script, as well as change the alphabetical order of the letters. In May of the same year, the III Kalmyk Regional Conference on Language and Writing, which was held in <a href="/wiki/Elista" title="Elista">Elista</a>, confirmed this decision. The alphabet took the following form:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197682–86_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов197682–86-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table style="font-family:Arial Unicode MS; font-size:1.4em; border-color:#000000; border-width:1px; border-style:solid; border-collapse:collapse; background-color:#F8F8EF">
<tbody><tr>

<p>The letter <i>Ь ь</i>, unlike most other Soviet Latinized alphabets, denoted palatalization.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In this form, the alphabet existed until 1938.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_Cyrillic_alphabet">Modern Cyrillic alphabet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Modern Cyrillic alphabet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the second half of the 1930s, the USSR began the process of translating scripts into Cyrillic. The Latin script was in turn <a href="/wiki/Cyrillisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrillisation">replaced</a> by another Cyrillic script in 1938. Initially, the Kalmyk Cyrillic alphabet included all the letters of the Russian alphabet, as well as <b>Ä ä, Гъ гъ, Дж дж, Нъ нъ, Ö ö, Ӱ ӱ</b>. In 1941, the alphabet was reformed again - the outline of additional letters was changed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEНоминханов1976130_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEНоминханов1976130-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> However, due to the <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Kalmyks" title="Deportation of the Kalmyks">deportation of the Kalmyks</a> that followed soon, the transition to a new version of the alphabet was carried out only after their rehabilitation - in the late 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> These script reforms effectively disrupted the Oirat literary tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The modern Cyrillic alphabet used for the Kalmyk language is as follows:
</p>

<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Tatar_alphabet" title="Tatar alphabet">Tatar alphabet</a> is identical to the Kalmyk alphabet (both featuring the same additional letters to the Russian one), Kalmyks using Windows use Tatar keyboard layouts to type Kalmyk. Kalmyk-specific keyboard layouts, however, are available on Android and Linux systems.
</p>

<p>* Pronounced /je/ at the beginning of words and /e/ otherwise. Only appears at the beginning of a word in Russian loanwords.<br />
** This sound combination exists in native Kalmyk words, but is spelled "йо".<br />
*** Only appears at the beginning of words.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Example_text">Example text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kalmyk_Oirat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Example text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This text is from <a href="/wiki/State_Anthem_of_the_Republic_of_Kalmykia" title="State Anthem of the Republic of Kalmykia">State Anthem of the Republic of Kalmykia</a>.
</p>

<td>Сарул сәәхн Хальмг Таңһч<br />
<p>Сансн тоотан күцәнә,<br />
Авта җирһлин бат җолаг<br />
Алдр һартан атхна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегән кеерүлий!<br />
Төрскн нутгтан күчән нерәдәд,<br />
Толһа менд җирһий!
</p><p>Олн келн-әмтнлә хамдан<br />
Уралан Таңһчин зүткнә<br />
Иньгллтин залин өндр герлд<br />
Иргч мана батрна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегән кеерүлий!<br />
Төрскн нутгтан күчән нерәдәд,<br />
Толһа менд җирһий!
</p><p>Баатр-чиирг үрдәр туурад,<br />
Буурл теемг өснә.<br />
Сурһуль-номдан килмҗән өдәг,<br />
Сул нерән дуудулна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегән кеерүлий!<br />
Төрскн нутгтан күчән нерәдәд,<br />
Толһа менд җирһий!<br />
</p>
</td>
<td>Сарул сääхн Хальмг Таңгч<br />
<p>Сансн тоотан күцäнä,<br />
Авта ӝирглин бат ӝолаг<br />
Алдр гартан атхна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегäн кеерӱлий!<br />
Тöрскн нутгтан кӱчäн нерäдäд,<br />
Толга менд ӝиргий!
</p><p>Олн келн-äмтнлä хамдан<br />
Уралан Таңгчин зӱткнä<br />
Иньгллтин залин öндр герлд<br />
Иргч мана батрна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегäн кеерӱлий!<br />
Тöрскн нутгтан кӱчäн нерäдäд,<br />
Толга менд ӝиргий!
</p><p>Баатр-чиирг ӱрдäр туурад,<br />
Буурл теемг öснä.<br />
Сургуль-номдан килмӝäн öдäг,<br />
Сул нерäн дуудулна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегäн кеерӱлий!<br />
Тöрскн нутгтан кӱчäн нерäдäд,<br />
Толга менд ӝиргий!<br />
</p>
</td>
<td>Сарул сddхн Хальмг Тангһч<br />
<p>Сансн тоотан кюцdнd,<br />
Авта джирһлин бат джолаг<br />
Алдр һартан атхна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегdн кеерюлий!<br />
Тvрскн нутгтан кючdн нерdдdд,<br />
Толһа менд джирһий!
</p><p>Олн келн-dмтнлd хамдан<br />
Уралан Тангһчин зюткнd<br />
Иньгллтин залин vндр герлд<br />
Иргч мана батрна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегdн кеерюлий!<br />
Тvрскн нутгтан кючdн нерdдdд,<br />
Толһа менд джирһий!
</p><p>Баатр-чиирг юрдdр туурад,<br />
Буурл теемг vснd.<br />
Сурһуль-номдан килмджdн vдdг,<br />
Сул нерdн дуудулна.
</p><p>Улан залата хальмг улс,<br />
Улата теегdн кеерюлий!<br />
Тvрскн нутгтан кючdн нерdдdд,<br />
Толһа менд джирһий!<br />
</p>
</td>
<td>Sarul səəxn Xalьmg Taꞑhç<br />
<p>Sansn tootan kycənə,<br />
Avta ƶirhlin ʙat ƶolag<br />
Aldr hartan atxna.
</p><p>Ulan zalata xalьmg uls,<br />
Ulata teegən keerylij!<br />
Tɵrskn nutgtan kyçən nerədəd,<br />
Tolha mend ƶirhij!
</p><p>Oln keln-əmtnlə xamdan<br />
Uralan Taꞑhcin zytknə<br />
Inьglltin zalin ɵndr gerld<br />
Irgç mana ʙatrna!
</p><p>Ulan zalata xalьmg uls,<br />
Ulata teegən keerylij!<br />
Tɵrskn nutgtan kyçən nerədəd,<br />
Tolha mend ƶirhij!
</p><p>Baatr-çiirg yrdər tuurad,<br />
Buurl teemg ɵsnə.<br />
Surhulь-nomdan kilmƶən ɵdəg,<br />
Sul nerən duudulna.
</p><p>Ulan zalata xalьmg uls,<br />
Ulata teegən keerylij!<br />
Tɵrskn nutgtan kyçən nerədəd,<br />
Tolha mend ƶirhij!<br />
</p>
</td>
<td>Sarul səəhn Haľmg Tañğç<br />
<p>Sansn tótan küţənə,<br />
Avta cirğlin bat colag<br />
Aldr ğartan athna.
</p><p>Ulan zalata haľmg uls,<br />
Ulata tégən kérüliy!<br />
Törksn nutgtan küçən nerədəd,<br />
Tolğa mend cirğiy!
</p><p>Oln keln-əmtnlə hamdan<br />
Uralan Tañğçin zütknə<br />
Iňgĺtin zalin öndr gerld<br />
Irgç mana batrna.
</p><p>Ulan zalata haľmg uls,<br />
Ulata tégən kérüliy!<br />
Törksn nutgtan küçən nerədəd,<br />
Tolğa mend cirğiy!
</p><p>Bátr-çírg ürdər túrad,<br />
Búrl témg ösnə.<br />
Surğuľ-nomdan kilmcən ödəg,<br />
Sul nerən dúdulna.
</p><p>Ulan zalata haľmg uls,<br />
Ulata tégən kérüliy!<br />
Törksn nutgtan küçən nerədəd,<br />
Tolğa mend cirğiy!<br />
</p>
</td>
<td>Bright and beautiful Kalmyk Republic<br />
<p>Fulfills everything it wishes for.<br />
It holds in its glorious hands<br />
Strong reins of harmonious life.
</p><p>Kalmyks with Ulan-Zala,<br />
Let's adorn our natal steppes!<br />
Let's devote our power to the homeland,<br />
and live long happily!
</p><p>With all the peoples of different languages,<br />
The Republic is pushing forward.<br />
In the high light of the friendship flame,<br />
Our future is getting stronger.
</p><p>Kalmyks with Ulan-Zala,<br />
Let's adorn our natal steppes!<br />
Let's devote our power to the homeland,<br />
and live long happily!
</p><p>Heroic children have succeeded,<br />
The steppe has emerged.<br />
Putting effort into learning,<br />
They're putting up the free name.
</p><p>Kalmyks with Ulan-Zala,<br />
Let's adorn our natal steppes!<br />
Let's devote our power to the homeland,<br />
and live long happily!<br />
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>

Межгосударственный совет по стандартизации, метрологии и сертификации.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%B0+%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%B8+%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE+%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BC%D0%B0+%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BC+%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BC&amp;rft.atitle=%D0%93%D0%9E%D0%A1%D0%A2+7.79-2000&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ifap.ru%2Flibrary%2Fgost%2F7792000.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AKalmyk+Oirat" class="Z3988"></span></span>
